					<div id="mw-content-text" class="mw-body-content mw-content-ltr" lang="en" dir="ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">American rapper (1985–2019)</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Not to be confused with comedian <a href="/wiki/Nipsey_Russell" title="Nipsey Russell">Nipsey Russell</a>.</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">

</p>

</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Website</th><td class="infobox-data"><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://ihussle.com">ihussle<wbr />.com</a></span></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2">
<div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Musical artist</div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Ermias Joseph Asghedom</b> (August 15, 1985 &#8211; March 31, 2019; born <b>Airmiess Joseph Asghedom</b>), known professionally as <b>Nipsey Hussle</b> (often stylized as <b>Nipsey Hu$$le</b>), was an American rapper, entrepreneur, and activist. Emerging from the <a href="/wiki/West_Coast_hip_hop" title="West Coast hip hop">West Coast hip hop</a> scene in the mid-2000s, Hussle independently released his debut <a href="/wiki/Mixtape" title="Mixtape">mixtape</a>, <i>Slauson Boy Volume 1</i>, to moderate local success, which led to him being signed to <a href="/wiki/Cinematic_Music_Group" title="Cinematic Music Group">Cinematic Music Group</a> and <a href="/wiki/Epic_Records" title="Epic Records">Epic Records</a>.
</p><p>Hussle became known for his numerous mixtapes, including his <i>Bullets Ain't Got No Name</i> series, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Marathon_(mixtape)" title="The Marathon (mixtape)">The Marathon</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Marathon_Continues" title="The Marathon Continues">The Marathon Continues</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Crenshaw_(mixtape)" title="Crenshaw (mixtape)">Crenshaw</a></i>, the last of which American rapper <a href="/wiki/Jay-Z" title="Jay-Z">Jay-Z</a> bought 100 copies for $100 each. After much delay, his debut studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Victory_Lap_(Nipsey_Hussle_album)" title="Victory Lap (Nipsey Hussle album)">Victory Lap</a></i> was released in 2018 to critical acclaim and commercial success, and was nominated for the <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Rap_Album" title="Grammy Award for Best Rap Album">Best Rap Album</a> at the <a href="/wiki/61st_Annual_Grammy_Awards" title="61st Annual Grammy Awards">61st Grammy Awards</a> in 2019. At the <a href="/wiki/62nd_Annual_Grammy_Awards" title="62nd Annual Grammy Awards">62nd Grammy Awards</a> in 2020, two posthumous <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Awards</a> for the songs "<a href="/wiki/Racks_in_the_Middle" title="Racks in the Middle">Racks in the Middle</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Higher_(DJ_Khaled_song)" title="Higher (DJ Khaled song)">Higher</a>" were awarded to Hussle in the <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Rap_Performance" title="Grammy Award for Best Rap Performance">Best Rap Performance</a> and <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Rap/Sung_Performance" class="mw-redirect" title="Grammy Award for Best Rap/Sung Performance">Best Rap/Sung Performance</a> categories respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Outside of music, Hussle inaugurated the Marathon Clothing store, which he founded along with partners Carless, the head of the agency, <a href="/wiki/Karen_Civil" title="Karen Civil">Karen Civil</a>, and his brother Samiel Asghedom in 2017, and started a <a href="/wiki/Co-working" class="mw-redirect" title="Co-working">co-working</a> environment which he named "Vector 90". On March 31, 2019, Hussle was fatally shot outside his store in <a href="/wiki/South_Central_Los_Angeles" class="mw-redirect" title="South Central Los Angeles">South Central Los Angeles</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Eric Holder, a 29-year-old man who confronted Hussle earlier that day, was arrested and charged with murder two days later.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Holder was found guilty of first-degree murder on July 6, 2022.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> On February 22, 2023, Holder was sentenced to 60 years to life in prison.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> 
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span></h2>
<p>Airmiess Joseph Asghedom<sup id="cite_ref-LA_Weekly_obit_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LA_Weekly_obit-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> was born on August 15, 1985, and raised in the <a href="/wiki/Crenshaw_District" class="mw-redirect" title="Crenshaw District">Crenshaw District</a> of <a href="/wiki/South_Central_Los_Angeles" class="mw-redirect" title="South Central Los Angeles">South Central Los Angeles</a><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> by his mother Angelique Smith (<span title="Name at birth"><a href="/wiki/Birth_name#Maiden_and_married_names" title="Birth name">née</a></span> Boutte), an African-American woman, and Dawit Asghedom, an Eritrean <a href="/wiki/War_refugee" class="mw-redirect" title="War refugee">war refugee</a> who came to the United States after fleeing a then ongoing <a href="/wiki/Eritrean_War_of_Independence" title="Eritrean War of Independence">Eritrean War of Independence</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-LAT_2019-04-08_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LAT_2019-04-08-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:0_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-usatoday_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usatoday-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> He was raised with his brother Samiel<sup id="cite_ref-usatoday_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usatoday-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Pseudonym" title="Pseudonym">a/k/a</a> Blacc Sam and his sister Samantha.<sup id="cite_ref-xxl_sister_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-xxl_sister-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Asghedom attended <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Hamilton_High_School_(Los_Angeles)" title="Alexander Hamilton High School (Los Angeles)">Alexander Hamilton High School</a> in the nearby <a href="/wiki/Castle_Heights,_Los_Angeles" title="Castle Heights, Los Angeles">Castle Heights</a> neighborhood, and dropped out before graduating.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>At age 14, Asghedom left home and joined the local <a href="/wiki/Rollin_60%27s_Neighborhood_Crips" class="mw-redirect" title="Rollin 60&#39;s Neighborhood Crips">Rollin 60's Neighborhood Crips</a>, a sub-group of the larger <a href="/wiki/Crips" title="Crips">Crips</a> gang primarily based in his home neighborhood of Crenshaw.<sup id="cite_ref-complex1_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-complex1-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> In 2002, at the age of 17, Hussle would join Buttervision, a creative multimedia <i>Digital Guerrilla</i> movement led by Dexter Browne where he would be part of the <i>BV Boys Sampler</i>, <i>Beats &amp; Babes Vol. 1</i> DVD, and <i>Shades of Butter Vol. 1</i> DVD. He would also get his name "Nipsey Hussle" there and complete the recording for his debut mixtape  <i>Slauson Boy Volume 1</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>His <a href="/wiki/Stage_name" title="Stage name">stage name</a>, a play on the name of comedian and game show panelist <a href="/wiki/Nipsey_Russell" title="Nipsey Russell">Nipsey Russell</a>, originated as a nickname given to Asghedom by a childhood acquaintance who respected his work ethic.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> In 2004, when Asghedom was 19, his father took him and his brother Samiel on a three-month trip to <a href="/wiki/Eritrea" title="Eritrea">Eritrea</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Asghedom credited the trip with inspiring him to become a <a href="/wiki/Community_activism" class="mw-redirect" title="Community activism">community activist</a> with an "<a href="/wiki/Entrepreneurship" title="Entrepreneurship">entrepreneurial</a> spirit".<sup id="cite_ref-LAT_2019-04-08_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LAT_2019-04-08-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-LAT_2019-04-02_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LAT_2019-04-02-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-complex1_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-complex1-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Music_career">Music career</span></h2>
<h3><span id="2008.E2.80.932010:_Bullets_Ain.27t_Got_No_Name_series"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2008–2010:_Bullets_Ain't_Got_No_Name_series">2008–2010: <i>Bullets Ain't Got No Name</i> series</span></h3>
<p>In December 2005, Hussle independently released his first mixtape, <i>Slauson Boy Volume 1</i>, to moderate local success.<sup id="cite_ref-:6_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:6-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> His debut project helped to build a small regional fanbase on the west coast, and eventually led to Hussle being signed to <a href="/wiki/Cinematic_Music_Group" title="Cinematic Music Group">Cinematic Music Group</a> and <a href="/wiki/Epic_Records" title="Epic Records">Epic Records</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-parle_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-parle-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-WCNN1_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WCNN1-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-XXLSept_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-XXLSept-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-auto4_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto4-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> In 2008, Hussle released the first two installments in his <i>Bullets Ain't Got No Name</i> series of mixtapes, which helped to bring Hussle's music to a larger audience.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Big_Sean_%26_Nipsey_Hussle.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Big_Sean_%26_Nipsey_Hussle.jpg/190px-Big_Sean_%26_Nipsey_Hussle.jpg" decoding="async" width="190" height="184" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Big_Sean_%26_Nipsey_Hussle.jpg/285px-Big_Sean_%26_Nipsey_Hussle.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Big_Sean_%26_Nipsey_Hussle.jpg/380px-Big_Sean_%26_Nipsey_Hussle.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1921" data-file-height="1856" /></a><figcaption>Nipsey Hussle (left) with rapper <a href="/wiki/Big_Sean" title="Big Sean">Big Sean</a> in 2009</figcaption></figure>
<p>Nipsey's profile continued to grow into 2009 when he collaborated with <a href="/wiki/Drake_(musician)" title="Drake (musician)">Drake</a> on the song "Killer",<sup id="cite_ref-WCNN_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WCNN-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> and also appeared, along with <a href="/wiki/Snoop_Dogg" title="Snoop Dogg">Snoop Dogg</a> and <a href="/wiki/Problem_(rapper)" title="Problem (rapper)">Problem</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-baller_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-baller-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> on the song "Upside Down",<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> from Snoop Dogg's 2009 album <i><a href="/wiki/Malice_n_Wonderland" title="Malice n Wonderland">Malice n Wonderland</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> He released the third installment in <i>Bullets Ain't Got No Name</i>, as well as his commercial debut single, "Hussle in the House". Despite the song, which samples <a href="/wiki/Kris_Kross" title="Kris Kross">Kris Kross</a>' 1992 single <a href="/wiki/Jump_(Kris_Kross_song)" title="Jump (Kris Kross song)">Jump</a>, being well received by critics, it failed to make any impact on the charts.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After Epic experienced financial issues in 2010, Nipsey opted not to renew his contract and left the label.<sup id="cite_ref-auto4_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto4-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Not long after going independent, Hussle appeared on the song "<a href="/wiki/We_Are_the_World_25_for_Haiti" title="We Are the World 25 for Haiti">We Are the World 25 for Haiti</a>",<sup id="cite_ref-XXLInterview_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-XXLInterview-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> and was featured by <i><a href="/wiki/XXL_Magazine" class="mw-redirect" title="XXL Magazine">XXL Magazine</a></i> as one of its "Annual Freshman Top Ten", a selection of ten up-and-coming hip-hop artists to watch.<sup id="cite_ref-XXL10_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-XXL10-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> XXL labeled him "Most Determined" of his class, and <i>LA Weekly</i> called him the "next big L.A. MC".<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-laweekly1_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-laweekly1-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Hussle was expected to release his debut album, <i>South Central State of Mind,</i> in October 2010. Prior to release, the album was supported by the single "<a href="/wiki/Feelin%27_Myself_(Nipsey_Hussle_song)" title="Feelin&#39; Myself (Nipsey Hussle song)">Feelin' Myself</a>" featuring <a href="/wiki/Lloyd_(singer)" title="Lloyd (singer)">Lloyd</a>. While the production was set to be handled from <a href="/wiki/J.R._Rotem" class="mw-redirect" title="J.R. Rotem">J.R. Rotem</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scott_Storch" title="Scott Storch">Scott Storch</a>, Mr. Lee, <a href="/wiki/Play-N-Skillz" title="Play-N-Skillz">Play-N-Skillz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Terrace_Martin" title="Terrace Martin">Terrace Martin</a>, and 1500 or Nothin', the album was set to be featured with the guest appearances from <a href="/wiki/Trey_Songz" title="Trey Songz">Trey Songz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jay_Rock" title="Jay Rock">Jay Rock</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sean_Kingston" title="Sean Kingston">Sean Kingston</a>. Concurrently, he announced that he planned on releasing a mixtape with fellow rapper Jay Rock, titled <i>Red and Blue Make Green</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> Following the release of a music video for "Feelin' Myself", the album was set for a December 21, 2010 release; however, both of these projects were eventually postponed indefinitely.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2010.E2.80.932013:_Leaving_Epic_Records_and_The_Marathon_series"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2010–2013:_Leaving_Epic_Records_and_The_Marathon_series">2010–2013: Leaving Epic Records and <i>The Marathon</i> series</span></h3>
<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Nipsey_Hussle_2013_December.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Nipsey_Hussle_2013_December.jpg/160px-Nipsey_Hussle_2013_December.jpg" decoding="async" width="160" height="230" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Nipsey_Hussle_2013_December.jpg/240px-Nipsey_Hussle_2013_December.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Nipsey_Hussle_2013_December.jpg/320px-Nipsey_Hussle_2013_December.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1270" data-file-height="1825" /></a><figcaption>Hussle performing in 2013</figcaption></figure>
<p>After leaving Epic, Nipsey founded his own record label, <a href="/w/index.php?title=All_Money_In_Records&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="All Money In Records (page does not exist)">All Money In Records</a><sup id="cite_ref-laweekly1_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-laweekly1-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> On December 21, 2010, he released his first <i>All Money In Records</i> mixtape, titled <i><a href="/wiki/The_Marathon_(mixtape)" title="The Marathon (mixtape)">The Marathon</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> which featured guest appearances from <a href="/wiki/Kokane" title="Kokane">Kokane</a> and <a href="/wiki/MGMT" title="MGMT">MGMT</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> On November 1, 2011, Hussle released a sequel titled <i><a href="/wiki/The_Marathon_Continues" title="The Marathon Continues">The Marathon Continues</a></i>, which featured L.A. rappers <a href="/wiki/YG_(rapper)" title="YG (rapper)">YG</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dom_Kennedy" title="Dom Kennedy">Dom Kennedy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> On April 17, 2012, Hussle released a collaborative album with fellow rapper Blanco, <i>Raw</i>. The album featured guest appearances from YG, <a href="/wiki/Mistah_FAB" class="mw-redirect" title="Mistah FAB">Mistah FAB</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yukmouth" title="Yukmouth">Yukmouth</a>, <a href="/wiki/B-Legit" title="B-Legit">B-Legit</a>, Kokane and <a href="/wiki/Freeway_(rapper)" title="Freeway (rapper)">Freeway</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In May 2012, Nipsey released a single titled <i>Proud of That</i>, marking his first collaboration with Florida rapper <a href="/wiki/Rick_Ross" title="Rick Ross">Rick Ross</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> Nipsey was subsequently featured on Ross' <a href="/wiki/Maybach_Music_Group" title="Maybach Music Group">Maybach Music Group</a>'s song "Fountain of Youth", which appears on the label's second album <i><a href="/wiki/Self_Made_Vol._2" title="Self Made Vol. 2">Self Made Vol. 2</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> The music video was released on October 1, 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> Rumours began to circulate that Nipsey would sign with MMG, and in December 2012, Hussle himself hinted at signing, however, he also said that he was still looking for the right label.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Hussle said that he would be releasing his third and final installment of <i>The Marathon</i> mixtape series with <i>TM3: Victory Lap</i> in 2013, after it was pushed back from its initial December 2012 release date.<sup id="cite_ref-www.hotnewhiphop.com_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-www.hotnewhiphop.com-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> He also announced that he was planning on releasing a joint mixtape with fellow West Coast rapper and frequent collaborator YG.<sup id="cite_ref-hiphopdx.com_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hiphopdx.com-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> Hussle performed at the 2013 <a href="/wiki/Paid_Dues" title="Paid Dues">Paid Dues</a> festival on March 30, 2013, in California.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> After deciding against signing to a major label, due to a lack of creative freedom, he choose to make <i>Victory Lap</i> his debut album.<sup id="cite_ref-complex.com_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-complex.com-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2013.E2.80.932019:_Crenshaw_and_Victory_Lap"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2013–2019:_Crenshaw_and_Victory_Lap">2013–2019: <i>Crenshaw</i> and <i>Victory Lap</i></span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Crenshaw_(mixtape)" title="Crenshaw (mixtape)">Crenshaw (mixtape)</a> and <a href="/wiki/Victory_Lap_(Nipsey_Hussle_album)" title="Victory Lap (Nipsey Hussle album)">Victory Lap (Nipsey Hussle album)</a></div>
<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Nipsey_Hussle.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Nipsey_Hussle.jpg/170px-Nipsey_Hussle.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Nipsey_Hussle.jpg/256px-Nipsey_Hussle.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Nipsey_Hussle.jpg/340px-Nipsey_Hussle.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1080" data-file-height="1440" /></a><figcaption>Hussle performing in 2014</figcaption></figure>
<p>Beginning in 2013, he released various songs from his upcoming mixtape <i><a href="/wiki/Crenshaw_(mixtape)" title="Crenshaw (mixtape)">Crenshaw</a></i>, including the <a href="/wiki/9th_Wonder" title="9th Wonder">9th Wonder</a> produced track "Face the World", and a <a href="/wiki/The_Futuristics" title="The Futuristics">Futuristics</a> and 1500 or Nothin'–produced track "Blessings".<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> On August 6, 2013, Hussle announced that <i>Victory Lap</i> would be released as an <a href="/wiki/Studio_album" class="mw-redirect" title="Studio album">album</a>, rather than a mixtape.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> Prior to the release of <i>Victory Lap</i>, Hussle announced on September 16, 2013, that he would be releasing a new mixtape, <i>Crenshaw</i> (hosted by <a href="/wiki/DJ_Drama" title="DJ Drama">DJ Drama</a>), on October 8, 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On September 24, 2013, he revealed the track list for <i>Crenshaw</i>, which contained guest appearances from Rick Ross, Dom Kennedy, <a href="/wiki/Slim_Thug" title="Slim Thug">Slim Thug</a>, <a href="/wiki/James_Fauntleroy_II" class="mw-redirect" title="James Fauntleroy II">James Fauntleroy II</a>, <a href="/wiki/Z-Ro" title="Z-Ro">Z-Ro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Skeme" title="Skeme">Skeme</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sade_(singer)" title="Sade (singer)">Sade</a>, among others. The production on the mixtape was handled by the Futuristics, 1500 or Nothin', <a href="/wiki/9th_Wonder" title="9th Wonder">9th Wonder</a>, Mike Free, Ralo and Jiggy Hendrix, among others. He also released the <i>Crenshaw</i> documentary that day in promotion of the mixtape.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> On October 3, 2013, he released another trailer for the mixtape, and attracted attention when he revealed 1,000 hard copies of the mixtape would be sold for $100 each. <a href="/wiki/Jay-Z" title="Jay-Z">Jay-Z</a> personally bought 100 copies.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> He reportedly sold out all 1,000 copies in less than 24 hours, effectively making $100,000.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Upon the release of <i>Crenshaw</i>, Hussle said that <i>Victory Lap</i> would be released in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> On November 20, 2013, Hussle confirmed that <i>Victory Lap</i> would feature production from Ralo, 1500 or Nothin', the Futuristiks and DJ Mustard.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> He later confirmed more producers, including <a href="/wiki/Don_Cannon" title="Don Cannon">Don Cannon</a> and <a href="/wiki/DJ_Khalil" title="DJ Khalil">DJ Khalil</a> on the album.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> After the year went by with no new releases, Hussle released a new mixtape, <i><a href="/wiki/Mailbox_Money_(mixtape)" title="Mailbox Money (mixtape)">Mailbox Money</a></i> on New Year's Eve 2014, again releasing 1000 hard copies for $100 each.<sup id="cite_ref-Guard_2015/jan/20_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guard_2015/jan/20-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Hussle made a number of guest appearances throughout 2015 and 2016, working with <a href="/wiki/Jadakiss" title="Jadakiss">Jadakiss</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trae_Tha_Truth" class="mw-redirect" title="Trae Tha Truth">Trae Tha Truth</a>, and <a href="/wiki/YG_(rapper)" title="YG (rapper)">YG</a>. In 2016, he released another mixtape, titled <i>Famous Lies and Unpopular Truth</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> He commented on the <a href="/wiki/2016_United_States_presidential_election" title="2016 United States presidential election">2016 US presidential election</a> by releasing the single "<a href="/wiki/FDT_(song)" title="FDT (song)">FDT</a>" ("Fuck <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a>") with YG; the song was written about Hussle's positive experiences with Mexican immigrants in the United States, whom Trump had criticized.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After numerous delays, Hussle's debut studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Victory_Lap_(Nipsey_Hussle_album)" title="Victory Lap (Nipsey Hussle album)">Victory Lap</a></i>, was released on February 16, 2018, debuting at number 4 on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a>, selling 53,000 album equivalent units in its first week.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> The album was met with universal acclaim from critics,<sup id="cite_ref-auto1_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Guardian_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Pitchfork_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pitchfork-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-auto2_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto2-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> and numerous songs entered the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a>, including "<a href="/wiki/Double_Up_(Nipsey_Hussle_song)" title="Double Up (Nipsey Hussle song)">Double Up</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Last_Time_That_I_Checc%27d" title="Last Time That I Checc&#39;d">Last Time That I Checc'd</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Dedication_(song)" title="Dedication (song)">Dedication</a>", marking Hussle's debut on the chart as a lead artist.<sup id="cite_ref-billboard.com_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-billboard.com-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i>Victory Lap</i> was nominated for a <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Rap_Album" title="Grammy Award for Best Rap Album">Best Rap Album</a> at the <a href="/wiki/61st_Annual_Grammy_Awards" title="61st Annual Grammy Awards">61st Annual Grammy Awards</a> in 2019, but lost to <a href="/wiki/Cardi_B" title="Cardi B">Cardi B</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Privacy_(album)" title="Invasion of Privacy (album)">Invasion of Privacy</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-auto3_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto3-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> Over 1 year after its release, the album reached a new peak of number 2 on the <i>Billboard</i> 200 in April 2019 after Hussle's murder on March 31. His single "<a href="/wiki/Racks_in_the_Middle" title="Racks in the Middle">Racks in the Middle</a>" featuring <a href="/wiki/Roddy_Ricch" title="Roddy Ricch">Roddy Ricch</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hit-Boy" title="Hit-Boy">Hit-Boy</a> debuted at number 44 on the Hot 100, following his death. The song later peaked at number 26.<sup id="cite_ref-billboard.com_73-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-billboard.com-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Business_ventures">Business ventures</span></h2>
<p>Hussle's nickname came from his entrepreneurial spirit. He shined shoes for $2.50 to pay for school clothes at age 11 with a goal of a hundred shoes a day.<sup id="cite_ref-LAT_2019-05-08_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LAT_2019-05-08-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> Hussle sold his mixtapes out of a car trunk at a neighborhood strip mall at the intersection of Slauson Avenue and Crenshaw Boulevard.<sup id="cite_ref-LAT_2019-04-04_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LAT_2019-04-04-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> After leaving Epic Records, he founded his own record label. Hussle experimented with unorthodox sales strategies by selling expensive copies of certain mixtapes even while the songs were distributed for free.<sup id="cite_ref-Guard_2015/jan/20_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guard_2015/jan/20-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Hussle's Marathon branding inspired Steve Carless in 2013 when he founded Marathon Agency with business partners <a href="/wiki/Karen_Civil" title="Karen Civil">Karen Civil</a> and Jorge Peniche. They designed the talent-based brand to attract a diverse set of clients in all stages of their careers. In October 2016, Carless, the head of the agency, told <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i> that Hussle had invested "like over six figures" in the Marathon Agency and described him as "kind of like our silent partner".<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Hussle opened the Marathon Clothing store on June 17, 2017, which he founded along with partners Carless, Civil, and his brother Samiel Asghedom.<sup id="cite_ref-:7_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:7-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> Opening the store at this intersection in the Crenshaw commercial district was important to him because he wanted to invest and provide opportunities in his neighborhood of <a href="/wiki/Hyde_Park,_Los_Angeles" title="Hyde Park, Los Angeles">Hyde Park</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-LAT_2019-04-02_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LAT_2019-04-02-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> The store is billed as a "smart store", which bridges the gap between culture and technology by giving customers access to exclusive music and other content created by rappers through an <a href="/wiki/Application_software" title="Application software">app</a> created by software engineer <a href="/wiki/Iddris_Sandu" title="Iddris Sandu">Iddris Sandu</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> The year before his death, Hussle bought the small shopping center where his store was located, after partnering with the real estate investor David Gross.<sup id="cite_ref-:5_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:5-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-LAT_2018-02-28_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LAT_2018-02-28-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-LAT_2019-05-08_77-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LAT_2019-05-08-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="All_Money_In">All Money In</span></h3>
<p>Hussle created the record label All Money In after leaving Epic Records.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> He released his first major project, <i>The Marathon</i>, through the new label on December 21, 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-laweekly1_35-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-laweekly1-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> He released subsequent projects under his label, including <i>The Marathon Continues</i> (2011), <i>Crenshaw</i> (2013), and <i>Mailbox Money</i> (2014). He also signed other artists, including J Stone, Pacman Da Gunman, BH, Cobby Supreme, Cuzzy Capone and Killa Twan.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dt>Releases</dt></dl>

</div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Acting">Acting</span></h2>
<p>In 2007, Hussle played a small role in <a href="/wiki/Bone_Thugs-n-Harmony" title="Bone Thugs-n-Harmony">Bone Thugs-n-Harmony</a>'s semi-autobiographical film <i>I Tried</i>, which was directed by <a href="/wiki/Rich_Newey" title="Rich Newey">Rich Newey</a>. In 2010, he starred in the film <i>Caged Animal</i>, alongside <a href="/wiki/Ving_Rhames" title="Ving Rhames">Ving Rhames</a>, Gillie Da Kid and <a href="/wiki/Robert_Patrick" title="Robert Patrick">Robert Patrick</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> In 2015, Hussle was featured in a <a href="/wiki/Cameo_appearance" title="Cameo appearance">cameo</a> "The Sexy Getting Ready Song" in the pilot episode of <i><a href="/wiki/Crazy_Ex-Girlfriend" title="Crazy Ex-Girlfriend">Crazy Ex-Girlfriend</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-:2_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> rapping two bars.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_92-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Community_activism">Community activism</span></h2>
<p>Hussle wanted to focus on "giving solutions and inspiration" to young black men like him.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> He denounced gun violence through his music, influence, and community work.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> He spoke openly about his experiences with gang culture.<sup id="cite_ref-BUS_2019/04/02_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BUS_2019/04/02-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> Affiliated with the Rollin' 60s, he often performed and worked with rival <a href="/wiki/Bloods" title="Bloods">Bloods</a>-affiliated rappers to set an example.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>He funded improvements to neighborhood schools and spent time with students, also participating on panels about growing up in the area and the influence of gang culture.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> Hussle started a <a href="/wiki/Co-working" class="mw-redirect" title="Co-working">co-working</a> environment which he named Vector 90.<sup id="cite_ref-LAT_2019-04-04_78-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LAT_2019-04-04-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> From his own experience, he believed that the Crenshaw area was being underserved and that young people would benefit from communal workspaces.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> He wanted youths to be able to take classes in <a href="/wiki/Science,_technology,_engineering,_and_mathematics" title="Science, technology, engineering, and mathematics">science, technology, and mathematics</a> at the center.<sup id="cite_ref-NBC_2019-04-01_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NBC_2019-04-01-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Hussle was also intimately involved in the planning and advisory stages of the <a href="/wiki/Destination_Crenshaw" title="Destination Crenshaw">Destination Crenshaw</a> project that will showcase the history and culture of blacks in his neighborhood.<sup id="cite_ref-TAN_2020-05-01_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TAN_2020-05-01-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> City Council member <a href="/wiki/Marqueece_Harris-Dawson" title="Marqueece Harris-Dawson">Marqueece Harris-Dawson</a> said Hussle was in the earliest conversations on the project and was an integral part of the project's branding.<sup id="cite_ref-Huff_2019-04-04_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Huff_2019-04-04-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> In March 2019, Hussle had contacted officials from the LAPD to arrange a meeting with him and <a href="/wiki/Roc_Nation" title="Roc Nation">Roc Nation</a> about what they could do to help prevent <a href="/wiki/Gang_violence" class="mw-redirect" title="Gang violence">gang violence</a> in South Los Angeles.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT_2019-04-19_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT_2019-04-19-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> The meeting had been scheduled to take place on April 1.
</p><p>Hussle was murdered on March 31. According to Los Angeles Police Commissioner <a href="/wiki/Steve_Soboroff" title="Steve Soboroff">Steve Soboroff</a>, department officials will meet with Hussle's representatives at a future date on these issues to continue the activist's work in his honor.<sup id="cite_ref-NBC_2019-04-01_100-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NBC_2019-04-01-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span></h2>
<p>Hussle and actress <a href="/wiki/Lauren_London" title="Lauren London">Lauren London</a> began dating in 2013. They had a son together in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> London has a child from a previous relationship with fellow rapper <a href="/wiki/Lil_Wayne" title="Lil Wayne">Lil Wayne</a>, while Hussle had a daughter from a previous relationship.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> He remained very involved in South Los Angeles with his businesses, charitable activities, and the homes of family and friends.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-OCW_2019-04-02_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OCW_2019-04-02-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> The locations for a magazine shoot were in the neighborhood.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT_2019/04/11_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT_2019/04/11-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Death">Death</span></h2>
<p>On March 31, 2019, Hussle was shot at least 10 times in the parking lot of his store, Marathon Clothing, in South Central Los Angeles at 3:18&#160;p.m. The perpetrator also kicked Hussle in the head.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> Two others were wounded in the shooting.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>All three victims were transported to a hospital, where Hussle was pronounced dead at 3:55&#160;p.m. He was 33 years old.<sup id="cite_ref-Coroner_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Coroner-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> Police identified then-29-year-old Eric Ronald Holder Jr. as the suspect.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> Investigators believed Holder was known to the rapper and that the shooting was possibly motivated by a personal matter.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> On April 2, 2019, Holder was arrested by the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Police_Department" title="Los Angeles Police Department">Los Angeles Police Department</a> and was being held in solitary confinement.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On May 9, a grand jury indicted Holder on one count of murder, two counts each of attempted murder and assault with a firearm, and one count of possession of a firearm by a felon. After a couple of postponements,<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> the trial got underway in mid-June, 2022.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> Los Angeles County Deputy District Attorney John McKinney served as the case's prosecutor, while Aaron Jansen served as head of the defense.<sup id="cite_ref-:8_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:8-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> Holder's attorneys argued that he did not intend to kill Hussle but had acted in the <a href="/wiki/Emotion" title="Emotion">heat of the moment</a>. McKinney argued, "He thought about it and he did it. That's all premeditated means. It doesn't mean he planned it for weeks".<sup id="cite_ref-:8_129-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:8-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> Testimony at the trial established that, immediately before Holder shot Hussle, the two men argued over a rumor that Holder had <a href="/wiki/Informant" title="Informant">cooperated with law enforcement</a> in an unrelated matter.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> On July 6, 2022, Holder was found guilty of first-degree murder and two counts of attempted voluntary manslaughter relating to injuries he caused to bystanders.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> On February 22, 2023, Superior Court Judge H. Clay Jack announced Holder's sentence of 60 years.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Hussle's brother, Samiel Asghedom, was appointed the permanent administrator of Hussle's estate.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Memorials">Memorials</span></h3>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Nipsey_Hussle_memorial_area.gif" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Nipsey_Hussle_memorial_area.gif/220px-Nipsey_Hussle_memorial_area.gif" decoding="async" width="220" height="275" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Nipsey_Hussle_memorial_area.gif/330px-Nipsey_Hussle_memorial_area.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Nipsey_Hussle_memorial_area.gif/440px-Nipsey_Hussle_memorial_area.gif 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="750" /></a><figcaption>Memorial in front of Marathon Clothing, where Hussle was fatally shot</figcaption></figure>
<p>Upon hearing the news of his death, numerous celebrities offered their condolences on social media.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> Los Angeles Mayor <a href="/wiki/Eric_Garcetti" title="Eric Garcetti">Eric Garcetti</a> also offered his condolences to Hussle's family.<sup id="cite_ref-LAW_2019-04-01_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LAW_2019-04-01-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Hussle's memorial service was held on April 11 at the <a href="/wiki/Staples_Center" class="mw-redirect" title="Staples Center">Staples Center</a> in Los Angeles, with tickets provided free of charge.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Former president <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> praised the rapper for his work in the community, writing in a tribute, "While most folks look at the Crenshaw neighborhood where he grew up and see only gangs, bullets, and despair, Nipsey saw potential".<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Former president of Iran <a href="/wiki/Mahmoud_Ahmadinejad" title="Mahmoud Ahmadinejad">Mahmoud Ahmadinejad</a> paid homage to the late rapper on his official Twitter profile. The conservative politician quoted Hussle's lyrics in a tweet reading "How can one take someone's life so easily? 'Baby Don't Cry Gotta Keep Your Head Up Even when The Road is Hard Never Give Up'".<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The 25.5-mile (41.0&#160;km) funeral procession to <a href="/wiki/Forest_Lawn_Memorial_Park_(Hollywood_Hills)" title="Forest Lawn Memorial Park (Hollywood Hills)">Forest Lawn Memorial Park</a> wound through the streets of South Central L.A. including <a href="/wiki/Watts,_Los_Angeles" title="Watts, Los Angeles">Watts</a>, where he spent some of his formative years.<sup id="cite_ref-ET_2019-04-11_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ET_2019-04-11-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Nation_of_Islam" title="Nation of Islam">Nation of Islam</a> provided security along the route that was "both respectful to the community and in a way that the community respects" according to <a href="/wiki/Melina_Abdullah" title="Melina Abdullah">Melina Abdullah</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-LAist_2019-04-11_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LAist_2019-04-11-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> Mourners gathered at the <a href="/wiki/Watts_Towers" title="Watts Towers">Watts Towers</a> along the route.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> The crowds lining the streets demonstrated the impact he had on this community.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_145-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:4_95-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Gang leaders saw how Hussle resonated with young gang members and used the opportunity to curtail violence in their own ranks. A cross-section of gangs marched together at a memorial for Hussle and later held summits between L.A. and Compton. Largely confined to black gangs, they agreed to stay away from each other's territory and stop shooting at people. The peacemaking, which was a cease fire and not a truce, included hundreds of gangs similar to the <a href="/wiki/Watts_truce" title="Watts truce">truces of 1992</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-LAT_2019-06-23_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LAT_2019-06-23-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Remembrance_and_tributes">Remembrance and tributes</span></h2>
<p>A petition was started to rename the intersection of <a href="/wiki/Slauson_Avenue" title="Slauson Avenue">Slauson Avenue</a> and <a href="/wiki/Crenshaw_Boulevard" title="Crenshaw Boulevard">Crenshaw Boulevard</a> near Hussle's store Marathon Clothing to "Nipsey Hussle Square". On the day of his funeral, the council announced it was set to be renamed Ermias "Nipsey Hussle" Asghedom Square to honor him and his contributions to the neighborhood.<sup id="cite_ref-:5_84-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:5-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> There has also been a push from the community to name the nearby <a href="/wiki/Hyde_Park_station_(Los_Angeles_Metro)" title="Hyde Park station (Los Angeles Metro)">Hyde Park station</a> after him, according to <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Metro_Rail" title="Los Angeles Metro Rail">Metro</a>. A ceremony dedicating the at-grade <a href="/wiki/Light_rail" title="Light rail">light rail</a> station on the <a href="/wiki/K_Line_(Los_Angeles_Metro)" title="K Line (Los Angeles Metro)">K Line</a> to him and the Crenshaw community was held August 6, 2022.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>There was a strong artistic response to Nipsey Hussle's death. Within a few months, over 50 <a href="/wiki/Murals_of_Los_Angeles" title="Murals of Los Angeles">murals</a> dedicated to the rapper were painted in the City of Los Angeles.<sup id="cite_ref-ABC_2019-04-24_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ABC_2019-04-24-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> One mural is in an alley near the strip mall where he was killed.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> Hussle's store has remained closed since his death.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Hussle was  honored with a star in the recording category of the <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Walk_of_Fame" title="Hollywood Walk of Fame">Hollywood Walk of Fame</a> in front of <a href="/wiki/Amoeba_Music" title="Amoeba Music">Amoeba Music</a> on August 15, 2022, the 37th anniversary of his birth.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> Councilmember Marqueece Harris-Dawson proclaimed the day Nipsey Hussle Day and handed the framed proclamation to Hussle's grandmother, Margaret Smith, who stood with Hussle's sister, Samantha, and his father, Dawit Asghedom.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Inspired by the books that Hussle mentioned in interviews, songs and motivational messages, local chapters of the Marathon <a href="/wiki/Book_discussion_club" title="Book discussion club">Book Club</a> have formed.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> The list includes self-help bestsellers, cult classics and little-known books by black authors.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Michelle_Obama" title="Michelle Obama">Michelle Obama</a> included "Hussle and Motivate" on her 2020 workout playlist.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On April 2, 2019, <a href="/wiki/National_Basketball_Association" title="National Basketball Association">NBA</a> player <a href="/wiki/Russell_Westbrook" title="Russell Westbrook">Russell Westbrook</a> notched the second <a href="/wiki/Triple-double" class="mw-redirect" title="Triple-double">20-20-20 game</a> in NBA history in honor of Hussle.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On March 6, 2020, metal band <a href="/wiki/Body_Count_(band)" title="Body Count (band)">Body Count</a> released their seventh studio album titled <i>Carnivore</i>. The album features a song titled "When I'm Gone", which was written for Nipsey Hussle<sup id="cite_ref-Wiederhorn_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wiederhorn-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> by the band's singer and rapper <a href="/wiki/Ice-T" title="Ice-T">Ice-T</a>. The song features a spoken introductory part in which Ice-T says of Hussle, "the outcry of love and support after his death was incredible, but it inspired me to write this song." The song also features guest vocalist <a href="/wiki/Amy_Lee" title="Amy Lee">Amy Lee</a> from the band <a href="/wiki/Evanescence" title="Evanescence">Evanescence</a> who is also credited by Ice-T as having co-written the song.<sup id="cite_ref-Wiederhorn_159-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wiederhorn-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Rapper <a href="/wiki/Snoop_Dogg" title="Snoop Dogg">Snoop Dogg</a> released the tribute song "Nipsey Blue" which is dedicated to Nipsey Hussle in 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Rapper <a href="/wiki/Big_Sean" title="Big Sean">Big Sean</a> announced the song "<a href="/wiki/Deep_Reverence" title="Deep Reverence">Deep Reverence</a>" in honor of Nipsey Hussle.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> The track was released in August 2020 and features Nipsey Hussle. The music video was released in March 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Puma_(brand)" title="Puma (brand)">Puma</a> released the Marathon Clothing collection in September 2019 with 100% of net proceeds to the Neighborhood 'Nip' Foundation.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> The AMB store opened in September 2019 on Crenshaw Boulevard. This is another clothing company founded by Hussle with Cobby Supreme who was one of his best friends and an artist.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Hussle's longtime friend and collaborator <a href="/wiki/YG_(rapper)" title="YG (rapper)">YG</a> dedicated his performance at the 2019 <a href="/wiki/Coachella_Valley_Music_and_Arts_Festival" class="mw-redirect" title="Coachella Valley Music and Arts Festival">Coachella Valley Music and Arts Festival</a> to the memory of Nipsey Hussle.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/2020_Grammy_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="2020 Grammy Awards">2020 Grammy Awards</a>, <a href="/wiki/DJ_Khaled" title="DJ Khaled">DJ Khaled</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kirk_Franklin" title="Kirk Franklin">Kirk Franklin</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Legend" title="John Legend">John Legend</a>, <a href="/wiki/Meek_Mill" title="Meek Mill">Meek Mill</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roddy_Ricch" title="Roddy Ricch">Roddy Ricch</a>, and <a href="/wiki/YG_(rapper)" title="YG (rapper)">YG</a> all gave tribute to Hussle in honor of his legacy.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The season 2 premiere of <a href="/wiki/The_CW" title="The CW">The CW</a> series <i><a href="/wiki/All_American_(TV_series)" title="All American (TV series)">All American</a></i> included a candlelight <a href="/wiki/Vigil" title="Vigil">vigil</a> at <a href="/wiki/Hyde_Park,_Los_Angeles" title="Hyde Park, Los Angeles">Hyde Park</a> with a <a href="/wiki/Eulogy" title="Eulogy">eulogy</a> by the character Flip Williams (played by Lahmard Tate). Tattoo artist Keenan Chapman painted a <a href="/wiki/Mural" title="Mural">mural</a> just for the episode. The series included "<a href="/wiki/Grinding_All_My_Life" class="mw-redirect" title="Grinding All My Life">Grinding All My Life</a>" in its pilot, and series star <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Ezra" title="Daniel Ezra">Daniel Ezra</a> was a fan. Characters from the series wore clothes from the Marathon store. Hussle had planned to appear in the season 1 finale but had "scheduling conflicts".<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> A documentary on Nipsey Hussle is in development at <a href="/wiki/Netflix" title="Netflix">Netflix</a>, and is set to be co-produced and directed by <a href="/wiki/Ava_DuVernay" title="Ava DuVernay">Ava DuVernay</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Rapper <a href="/wiki/Kendrick_Lamar" title="Kendrick Lamar">Kendrick Lamar</a> paid tribute to Nipsey Hussle on the single "<a href="/wiki/The_Heart_Part_5" title="The Heart Part 5">The Heart Part 5</a>". The music video shows Hussle <a href="/wiki/Deepfake" title="Deepfake">deepfaked</a> on to Lamar's face as he rapped about his legacy following his death.
</p>
